Free Talk

A Word of Wisdom 141

— Holding to Buddhism

People's individualities vary infinitely. Forgive their shortcomings and cherish their strengths, and the world will be full of good people.

In life, there are favorable circumstances and unfavorable circumstances. It's like writing an essay: if there is only praise and no criticism, it cannot be a good essay. Therefore, being able to handle adversity has its own flavor.

Whenever starting something or establishing a career, one should first consider what the highest purpose is and what the consequences of failure would be. After carefully weighing the advantages and disadvantages, the undertaking will surely be accomplished and valuable.

From a young age, children should be taught the virtue of thrift and the difficulties of life; otherwise, they will surely experience great suffering and learn hard lessons. Even if they don't become dissolute, they will inevitably go through this process.

Being eccentric and disregarding customs is not the way to live in the world. There may be hidden dragons, but few who seek them out three times.

The way to nourish the mind, cure illness, live in the world, and conduct oneself lies in focusing on the word "qi." The effect is truly remarkable.

If one loves their parents as much as they love their wife, there will surely be no acts of disobedience. Thinking of where I came from, even if my parents unreasonably scold, humiliate, or beat me, I will gladly accept it.

Most men love women because they want to satisfy their sexual desires. That's why there are so many cases of starting with love and ending with abandonment. Even someone as talented and beautiful as Shuangwen is one of the ill-fated characters in history. Therefore, how should women carefully protect their lives?

When a wife is beautiful, her flaws will inevitably be discovered over time. When a wife is ugly, it seems that even in her ugliness there are beautiful aspects.

The Pioneer of the Revolutionary Army's Air Force 142

— Li Qingduo

Since the National Revolutionary Army set out from Guangdong, they have repeatedly defeated strong rebels and recovered the southeastern provinces. In every battle, the air force played a role in reconnaissance and bombing. Recently, when the Revolutionary Army recovered Jinan, the air force first flew over and bombed the enemy. Their contribution was great. Many people know the effectiveness of airplanes, but few know who founded the air force. Who is this person? It is Li Qi'an, the current member of the Overseas Chinese Affairs Committee of the Central Party Department. Li has been engaged in revolution for thirty years. Before the Restoration, Li was still in America. At that time, the manufacture of airplanes was still in its infancy. Li realized that airplanes were an indispensable weapon in the Revolutionary Army, so he sent a letter from America to Sun Yat-sen, suggesting the organization of an air force for aerial combat. Sun Yat-sen replied approvingly. Li then gathered comrades in America, raised funds to purchase four airplanes, and brought them back to China to assist in military operations. After the Restoration, the Provisional Government was established in Nanjing, and Sun Yat-sen was elected as the Provisional President. Li was then appointed as the captain of the air force. This was the first time the Revolutionary Army organized an air force, and Li was the first captain of the air force. From then on, aviation talents gradually returned from overseas, and the air force gradually expanded. Now the National Government's Aviation Administration has organized seven air force teams. Li, with the passage of time and changing circumstances, stopped his aviation life many years ago. He has now changed his position to a member of the Central Overseas Chinese Affairs Committee. But Li's aviation qualifications have not diminished in the slightest.

News from the Old Capital 143

— Tuo Ru

Mei Lanfang's Aunt's Funeral: Mei Lanfang, who returned with honors from performing in America, had his aunt, Madam Hu, pass away on August 4th at her residence on Wuliangdaren Hutong in the East City of Beiping. Many famous actors and those who had friendships with Mei went to pay their respects. The funeral was very grand. On the 12th, the funeral procession was held. The crowds of spectators along the way were immense. The coffin was carried by sixty-four pallbearers, covered with an embroidered red cover, which was quite dignified and beautiful. The ceremonial guards included monks, Taoists, and Buddhist scriptures, three bands of music, a group of Qingyin music, four pairs of flower pots, four pairs of musical fairies (all exquisitely made of paper), hundreds of pairs of snow willows, more than five hundred wreaths, forty pieces of mourning couplets, and flower baskets, etc. Those who held the ropes for the coffin were all famous actors and Mei's relatives and friends, and there were quite a few people. It is said that Mei did not use large gongs and other traditional instruments, but adopted foreign funeral methods.

Police Bureau Disguise Competition: Wang Xifu, the director of the Beiping Police Bureau, recently ordered the chiefs, police, and detectives of the fifteen districts in the inner and outer cities to compete in disguises at the bureau's parade ground in order to investigate important cases due to the unstable local situation and the ease with which bandits cause trouble. There were as many as 360 people in disguise. The disguises included blind people, villagers on their way, female receptionists, male and female students, fashionable girls, peanut vendors, monks, lamas, Taoists, nuns, farmers, Boy Scouts, shoemakers, carpenters, tilers, bowl menders, erhu players, drummers, wind instrumentalists, porters, beggars, coal ball and waste paper pickers, knife sharpeners, barbers, egg sellers, vegetable and flower sellers, newspaper sellers, summer medicine sellers, rickshaw pullers, singers, fortune tellers, cooks, etc., not less than thirty kinds. They were bizarre and varied. There were thousands of visitors, and no one did not laugh. Director Wang also instructed the judges to give awards according to the quality of the performance in order to encourage them.

Art and Buddhist Sayings 144

— Zhou Yuanqi

The autumn heat is oppressive, and I spend my days lying under the north window, reading paintings and reciting poems. Then I received a letter from Qian Huahuo, informing me that he was hosting the Art and Epigraphy Exhibition at the Yuncai Gallery on Nanjing Road and Yunnan Road. I braved the heat to visit my old friend at the exhibition, where we chatted and laughed happily. The four walls of the exhibition were almost entirely covered with paintings. Among them, Zeng Nongran's landscape painting in the style of Mi Fu was solid and yet had a rugged strength. This old gentleman is known throughout the country for his calligraphy, but his paintings are overshadowed by his calligraphy. In fact, this old gentleman's paintings are like Lin Qin'nan's literary works. Miao Pusun, known as Lishan Shanren, painted a chrysanthemum, with extremely exquisite and refined brushstrokes and balanced colors. He also inscribed it with the line: "No guests appreciate the flowing spring on the stone, only a few cold chrysanthemums understand its sound." I couldn't help but exclaim at this wonderful composition. Other works, such as Zhang Yuguang's tiger, Huang Binhong's landscape, and Liu Haisu's portrait, totaled more than thirty pieces, all of which were exquisite masterpieces. I heard Huahuo say that these thirty masterpieces will only be on display for three days. After that, Huahuo will hold a solo exhibition of Buddhist paintings, as well as an exhibition of calligraphy by Yang Du, who was famous during the Hongxian era. What is most noteworthy is that they are soliciting works from people in the old and new opera circles who are skilled in calligraphy and painting, such as Feng Zihe, Jin Biyan, Zheng Zhengqiu, Jia Biyun, Li Junpan, Wang Yunfang, Hu Hensheng, Huang Yulin, and Chen Jialin, each producing several pieces for an exhibition of calligraphy and painting by performers from the old and new opera circles. Among them, Jin Biyan's paintings of horses, Huang Yulin's clerical script, and Jia Biyun's landscapes are all rare works. I imagine it will cause a sensation. Huahuo also said that he has a large collection of cigarette lighters and cigarette pack labels, and he is planning to solicit others who specialize in collecting these unimportant items to hold a joint exhibition, refreshing the eyes and ears of the people of Shanghai. My friend Wang Zhongxian, who is known for his collection of painting fragments, is eager to try it out after hearing this news. It is said that Mr. Ge Gongzhen of this newspaper specializes in collecting newspapers from various countries. If they are combined for exhibition, it will also be a grand sight. Huahuo said that the name of this exhibition must have a unique flavor. He initially thought of the words "scrap paper basket," but Huahuo thought that "odds and ends" exhibition was better. This type of exhibition is not limited by any standard of what collections should be displayed. If one has old objects, such as fans, pouches, or snuff bottles, they can all be added. Huahuo spoke with great relish and offered Longjing's Biluochun tea, the fragrance permeating the spleen. Therefore, there is no need for Lu Tong's three paths. I had other important matters, so I couldn't listen to Huahuo's wonderful words any longer. I returned and wrote as follows.

Record of a Dragon Appearing in Lake Ge 145

— Tang Mei

Leaving Biling's west gate and heading south for thirty li, there is Lake Ge. It is a vast expanse of water, a hazy and misty sight. The scenery of this watery region has a unique charm. Lu Fan of the Ming dynasty wrote poems about Lake Ge, and Tang Qin composed lyrics about the autumn moon over the lake. The north and south sides are about a hundred li apart, and the east and west are thirty-five li. The lake is abundant with white fish and is bordered by Yixing in the middle. The mist is often so thick that mirages are visible. Legend has it that a family named Ge lived here and brought back a dragon egg, causing the land to sink and form the lake, hence the name. Recently returning to my hometown, I happened to meet my old friend Mr. Wang Huaisheng on the Shanghai-Nanjing road. While chatting over tea in the car, he told me about the dragon appearing on the lake, and after confirming its antiquity, it was truly astonishing. Having ample time as a copyist, I took up my pen to record it.

Mr. Wang's home is by the shore of Lake Ge. A stream of misty water flows right outside his door. The green hills of Lake Ge's bank are faintly visible in the distance. Sails rise and fall, and birds compete to sing. The scenery is picturesque and worthy of appreciation. The winding boat songs in the morning and evening, and the unpitched fisherman's flute, often complement the sound of reading. He considers this to be the ultimate joy. One day, it was a long summer's day with sultry weather. The scorching sun was in the sky, and woodcutters and fishermen had temporarily stopped working. Some were taking naps like Zai Yu, while others rested under trees like Feng Yi. Even the cicadas singing in the treetops seemed to be affected by the heat, stopping their songs. At this time, everything was silent, almost like a dark night. The driving force of heaven and earth was only the swarms of dragonflies flying gracefully. Suddenly, a strong wind arose, and dark clouds gathered from all directions. A tail appeared in the sky, hanging down into the center of the lake. Clouds and mist surged, and the scales of a dragon shimmered. Lake water splashed in all directions, swirling upwards. Neighbors ran to tell each other, astonished and bewildered. At that time, two large boats were sailing past. One was driven by the wind into a small harbor, while the other had its mast broken and the hull overturned. A torrential rain suddenly arrived, as if pouring from a basin. After about a meal's time, it moved towards the opposite shore, rising slowly, and the rain stopped immediately. Suddenly, the sky felt clear and the air was fresh, and the summer heat dissipated. The willow branches on the lake were newly green, and the water was as smooth as a mirror. The scenery after the rain was even more beautiful. Several friends, wanting to explore the extraordinary event, eagerly rowed a small boat to track it across the lake. They saw that where the dragon's body had passed, it stretched for three or four li, with houses collapsing and crops flattened. The width was about ten feet, like a roadway. Its end point was the Dragon King Temple. Mr. Wang originally did not believe that dragons existed in this world, but having witnessed this scene, what could he doubt?

Xiumei said, "The dragon is the leader of scaled creatures, one of the four spiritual beings. In ancient times, there were even officials in charge of raising dragons. The records in the classics are numerous and verifiable. Even today, geological studies examining fossils in the ground have confirmed that they were the largest animals of ancient times. However, they have long disappeared from the world. As for the distant sightings of dark, wriggling shadows near the sea, commonly called 'hanging dragons,' they are actually a type of hurricane that carries water upwards. However, Mr. Wang is a sincere scholar, and the event was witnessed firsthand, so his words should not be false. Could it be that the legend of the Ge family's dragon egg is not without reason? This is truly extraordinary."

Acknowledgement: But Duyu's collection of photographs, "Crystal of Beauty," captures both landscapes and still life perfectly. There are also dozens of photographs by Ms. Tan Xuerong, lively and fragrant, especially beautiful. Added to this are the inscriptions by Xu Zhenya and Zheng Yimei, making it needless to say how precious it is. I received a copy as a gift yesterday and would like to express my gratitude and introduce it on your behalf.

The Origin of the French Concession in Shanghai (Part 2) 146

— Translated by Ji Ping from the "North-China Herald"

In addition, the only astronomical observatory in China was built. The predictions published by this observatory were highly trusted by merchants navigating the Chinese coast. Before the French Concession became a ceded territory, there were many debates. In the past, there was a guild hall for the Chinese within the concession, as well as a place to keep coffins, namely the "Bingshe." There was also a public cemetery for burying those who could not afford burial grounds. In 1863, the guild hall and cemetery were located within the boundaries crossed by the French Concession. In 1865, there were plans to add roads. In 1870, a map of the proposed roads was published. The French Municipal Council decided to build certain roads, but the Siming Public Hall pointed out that if the roads were built according to the proposed map, their approved cemetery would be divided. The two sides argued endlessly, resulting in a riot. Chinese people set fire to many foreign residences. Although no foreigners were killed, there was a constant sense of danger. Several people were seriously injured. Seven Chinese people died and twelve were injured. As a result, the French consul allowed the Siming Public Hall and cemetery to remain untouched to settle the matter. However, this was overturned in 1898. The originally planned roads had already been built.

After this incident, the French built various roads according to their wishes within their concession and worked hard to manage it, turning the concession into the best residential area. Many British and Americans chose to build houses there, ignoring their own national concession. Furthermore, there were not many French people moving into the concession. In recent years, the French Concession has progressed rapidly. Many new roads and modern buildings have been built. Avenue Joffre is the most French-style avenue. The area nearby, such as Rue Cardinal Mercier, Avenue Albert, and Route Pichon, has gradually become the center of the French Concession. Not only are French businesses concentrated here, but international businesses are also conducted here. Many members of the French Cercle Sportif Français are British. The towering building called Cathay Mansions houses people from various countries. In addition to this, there are currently two large theaters under construction, one being the Lyceum Theatre opposite the French Club, and the other being the Carlton Theatre on Avenue Joffre. The French Cercle Sportif Français is the largest social center in Shanghai, due to its large tennis courts, swimming pool, and balconies. It has members from various countries. Dog and horse racing are nearby. In addition to the French Cercle Sportif Français, there are two clubs, one being the French Club and the other being the Police Club. The French Concession has its own tram, electricity, and water plants, and is not affiliated with the International Settlement. The French water and electricity plants have contributed greatly to the prosperity of the French Concession. There are many schools in the French Concession, making significant contributions to education and culture. Many have received high praise. St. Joseph's School is directly supervised by St. Joseph's Church. Aurora University is strictly managed and has cultivated many talented individuals. The Municipal Council operates two schools, one being the French School on Rue du Koukling and the other being the Franco-Chinese School on Baikal Road. In addition, there are St. Francis Xavier's School, Xuhui College, and schools run by the Catholic Church. Statistics published by the French Chamber of Commerce in China show the rise and prosperity of French society. There are a total of 6,704 French residents in China, with one-fifth of them residing in Shanghai. There are a total of 246 French businesses in China, with 125 in Shanghai, which is not a small number.

European Travelogue (69) 147

— Liu Haisu

Visiting the Palace of Versailles (Part 4)

For the panoramic view of the Palace of Versailles and its gardens, it is best to stand on the highest level of the main palace and look down. You can see the large white stone platform in front of the main palace, resembling the one in front of the Hall of Supreme Harmony in Beijing. In the front part, there are two large fountains surrounded by many bronze statues of male, female, old, and young water gods. The water sprays fiercely like clouds and mist. Various exotic flowers and trees are planted on the left and right, forming different shapes. Descending ten steps leads to the ground level. In the center is the Latona Fountain, Bassinde Latone. In the middle, there is a nude female statue, which is the statue of the goddess Latona. Latona is the mother of the god Apollo. —I should mention that the Latona Fountain is very grand. The circular stone platform in the middle has five layers. On top of each layer stands a stone-carved angel and a bronze-cast monster, all spouting water in different directions like mist and waves from their mouths. Dozens of water sprays erupt simultaneously. Anyone would marvel at this spectacle. Countless stone statues surround it. Flowers and stone steps encircle it from above and below. Trees surround the flowers, and the trees are tall and trimmed flat, stretching for more than ten li, dense and uniform. In front of the Latona Fountain is the green lawn stretching for ten li, with white stones lining the path. Every ten steps there are rows of stone statues. At the end of the green lawn is the Apollo Fountain, Bassin d'Apollon, filled with clear water, reflecting the azure sky. In the center, the god Apollo drives four galloping horses. This is a famous French sculpture. The characteristic of this sculpture is that it expresses the instantaneous movement of the god Apollo. His body leans forward, and his head faces upwards, as if gazing at the light of the sun. His right hand tightly grips the reins, and his left hand faces backwards, forming a direct opposition to his right hand. Therefore, the rapid movement of the body is fully expressed. The four horses, under the rapid control of the god Apollo, run wildly on the water in a violent rage. This posture expresses an instant of movement, achieving a full effect. During the height of the reign of Louis XIV, more than fifty sculptors gathered in the Palace of Versailles, specializing in the production of decorations for the palace and gardens. Therefore, wherever we go in Versailles today, we always see very beautiful and grand sculptures. I believe that no royal palace in Europe or America can compare to it. Even the Forbidden City in Beijing, China, although grand and solemn, does not have the sculptures that fill the Palace of Versailles and its gardens. The Apollo Fountain faces the palace a hundred feet away. Further ahead, there is a long stream stretching for several li. Trees line both sides, reaching the sky. Large roads are opened within them, and cars can drive around. The garden covers thousands of acres and is divided into four seasons. There are eighty fountains. Looking back from the end of the long stream, the green sky stretches as far as the eye can see, and the hills are endless. The magnificent and open scenery is truly astonishing.

Last Week's Drastic Changes in the Gold Market 148

Fierce and Terrifying

Falling Despite Weakness

Fluctuations Reached 36.2 Taels

The fluctuations in the Shanghai gold market last week were dramatic, chaotic, and unpredictable. The situation was extremely complex and unstoppable. Daily fluctuations ranged from 10 to over 20 taels, with rapid rises and falls. Dealers seemed lost, unable to make sense of the situation. The downward trend that started at the beginning of the week intensified rapidly, breaking through the 530 tael mark, almost in freefall. By Thursday, it had dropped to 529 taels, mainly because even though "Da Tiao" (silver bars for delivery) shrank, silver prices rose. Additionally, large sellers dumped their holdings, triggering the decline. Towards the weekend, foreign speculators like George Joege made large purchases to cover short positions and reversed to long positions. As a result, the exchange rate trend became tight, and the silver market was expected to shrink. Market sentiment was particularly positive, and it quickly rebounded, exceeding the 560 tael mark. The market appeared optimistic. However, short sellers had to cover their positions at a loss, causing significant impact and widespread concern. The difference between the highest and lowest prices during the week was 36.2 taels. Da Tiao rose by a total of half a cent, and the exchange rate rose by 1.5 points, to 1 shilling and 375 pence. As for the various dealers, many still had outstanding September contracts that had not been settled. In recent days, they have been gradually settling them, but the buyers have arbitrarily raised prices, reaching more than 10 to 20 taels. Otherwise, they would have to pay in cash at maturity. Given the shortage of spot gold in the market, those who were short faced immense pressure. The spot price was more than 20 taels higher than the market price, which was considered exorbitant. The dramatic changes in the market were impossible to predict. Here is a summary of the events that took place from Monday, August 18th to Saturday, August 23rd:

Result: Still Down 2.1 Taels

Starting from Monday, August 18th, Da Tiao silver had slightly recovered, and the exchange rate trend was weakening. In the gold market, October was strong in the morning but weak later. The afternoon market fell sharply by more than 20 taels due to Hengxingshengda and others selling, as well as news of cash export restrictions in Japan. The closing price was 43-44 taels. The next day, the silver market continued to rise, and the exchange rate rose sharply by 2 points. Therefore, the Shanghai gold market fell in early trading, breaking the 40 tael mark. Later, buying activity increased, and the London exchange rate turned from weak to stable, rebounding by 10 taels, reaching 47-48 taels. On Wednesday, the market situation was chaotic and turbulent, uncontrollable. However, because Da Tiao remained unchanged in the morning, and the silver market shrank, sentiment softened. It fell in early trading and dropped more than 10 taels from morning to noon. After 10 o'clock, it once fell to just over 50 taels. In the afternoon, rumors of the Central Bank selling spot gold caused panic among the long positions, and it suddenly dropped to 32-33 taels. The afternoon market seemed to ease, rebounding by 4-5 taels, but without significant changes, only fluctuating by 7-8 taels. The total fluctuation for the day was 20 taels. The next day, Da Tiao contracted, but the exchange rate eased, and the gold market rebounded by 10 taels. The morning market once broke into 530 taels, reaching 29 taels. Later, Hengxingshengda, Xinxing, and others bought in, recovering by 10 taels, resulting in a range of 37 taels, slightly down 7 cents from the previous day. On Friday, Da Tiao rose again, and the exchange rate improved. Therefore, the Shanghai gold market showed signs of rising. However, the fluctuation was only about 9 taels, hovering around 40 taels. Dealers such as Yuanxing and Yongyuansheng covered their short positions, and it jumped from 39 taels to 47-48 taels. On Saturday, the market situation continued to improve, with large buyers covering short positions and foreign firms also reversing to long positions. Sentiment strengthened, showing signs of soaring. It quickly broke through the 60 tael mark. The difference within half a day was 14-15 taels. However, Da Tiao weakened, and the London exchange rate contracted by half a point, and the domestic market was also tight. At noon, it reached 62 taels, and the closing price was 61 taels and 7 cents. Later, it rose by another 1-2 taels. Short sellers were eager to cover their positions, but they were under immense pressure, suffering heavy losses. It soared by 14 taels and 1 cent compared to the previous day, and a total of 25 taels compared to last Monday (Saturday). However, it was still down 2.1 taels compared to last Saturday. The initial discount for spot gold against the Shanghai gold market price was over 80 taels, but it gradually decreased to around 50 taels by the weekend. Last Week, the Yarn Market Initially Declined and then Became Obscure 154

The yarn market showed considerable unease at the beginning of the week, mainly because the overseas raw cotton market experienced a consistently sharp decline. Buyers were wary due to the unfavorable environment and anticipated a persistent downward trend in yarn prices. Consequently, they hesitated to make purchases, leading to a quiet sales environment. However, the Tianjin Gaoyang merchant group absorbed a large batch of 20-count "Blue Phoenix" yarn futures, approximately 5,000 bales, purely for speculative purposes. Yet, actual sales remained stagnant, resulting in a calm market sentiment. Buyers, observing the overall market trend, adopted a wait-and-see attitude. Nevertheless, the Chaozhou merchant group reversed positions by selling over 10,000 bales within these few days. Subsequently, by Wednesday and Thursday, American cotton prices stabilized somewhat, and the downward trend subsided. Due to reduced production, the market for third-grade yarn was relatively stable. A certain manufacturer and the Guangdong merchant group released near-month contracts and purchased far-month contracts, causing a slight increase in market prices. Simultaneously, outward sales became more active. Currently, the yarn market is higher than the cotton market; however, sellers also have strong influence, with both buyers and sellers possessing considerable strength. The future direction depends on actual demand. It is noted that total purchases by various merchant groups for the entire week amounted to 15,225 bales, including 6,000 to 7,000 bales of futures by Tianjin, inland areas, and Shantou, and 3,970 bales by fellow traders. The weekend saw a rise of one or two taels in Japanese yarn prices. Marked yarn initially followed the decline in foreign cotton, but then rebounded due to strong buying pressure. The lowest price for October contracts reached 154 taels and three mace. Consequently, prices for all months were down seven or eight mace compared to the previous week. Total transaction volume for the week was 120,050 bales. The prices paid by various merchant groups are recorded on the left:

Last Week, the Cotton Market Was Depressed by American Cotton 155

American cotton experienced a sharp decline, reaching the lowest price in several years, with spot prices reaching 11 cents. This situation was entirely due to the smooth progress of the new cotton harvest and a sharp reduction in consumption. Disappointed buyers triggered a significant drop. Although local cotton had the support of the Ningbo merchant group and strong buying pressure, the overall trend was difficult to resist. Small investors became fearful and had to cut their losses, resulting in a very weak market situation. This month, buying companies were unable to provide support, and most had to watch prices fall to 31 taels. Selling pressure intensified, and the buying side attempted to transfer 35,000 piculs to a certain manufacturer at a price of 32.5 taels, while simultaneously purchasing futures within a price limit of 3 taels. As a result, the market was temporarily supported, and the short-term panic subsided. Far-month contracts also fluctuated, with the lowest price for October reaching 32 taels and 2.5 mace. Market sentiment strengthened slightly at the weekend. However, a certain manufacturer continued to sell heavily to close out positions within a price limit of 3 taels. With favorable weather for the new cotton crop and abundant harvests in various regions, manufacturers rarely sold new cotton due to sufficient inventories of old cotton. The future of the cotton market depends on the weather and the price of American cotton. Prices for marked cotton across all months fell by eight to nine mace to one tael compared to the previous week. Total transaction volume for the week was 470,500 piculs. It is noted that the total transaction volume in the Hankou marked cotton futures market was 430,000 piculs, with both buyers and sellers remaining firm. Significant changes are expected to occur in the future. American cotton prices fell another 35 points this week. Manufacturers imported 22,800 piculs of Indian cotton, 1,960 piculs of local cotton, and trading houses imported 1,560 piculs. Grains: The Heshia Rice Market is Consistently Declining 156

Yesterday, over ten merchants from various regions arrived in Zhabei, but sales were extremely sluggish. High-quality and fresh Bei merchants' polished rice were down slightly by nearly one jiao. The opening price for large quantities was 20 yuan and seven or eight jiao. Medium and lower-grade polished rice were down by another one or two jiao. The market situation showed consistent weakness. Currently, stocks from the countryside will gradually be transported to Shanghai for sale, and local stockpilers also intend to sell. Therefore, the prospects for polished rice will only improve with a significant change in circumstances; otherwise, prices will continue to decline. The downward trend for thin rice has stabilized. Arrivals seem dry, and demand is acceptable, so prices have softened slightly by five fen to one jiao. Top-quality rice opened at 20 yuan and nine jiao. Since the previous night, Dongxin polished rice has fallen to 18.5 yuan, and the market has temporarily stabilized. However, the supply of this variety is abundant, making it difficult to maintain the current price level. Demand for new Kejian rice is sluggish, and arrivals are continuous, so prices are hovering around 14 yuan. The Bianyuan market continues to be weak, mainly due to slow sales, so prices have fallen by another jiao, with high-quality rice opening at 18 yuan and seven or eight jiao.

Su-Tong machine-milled polished rice has a slight market presence, and the market is generally weak. Ordinary high-quality rice opened at around 19 yuan, with very few transactions. The Nan merchant group's thin early rice market is clear, with no significant price fluctuations, around 20 yuan and six jiao. Sales of scattered Baiyuan are slightly active, with a weak situation. High-quality rice barely opened at 18 yuan and two or three jiao. Overall, the rice market here was quiet with few transactions, unlike the active market in the north.

Silk and Tea: Last Week, the Silk Market Trended Poorly 158

World Economy Declining… Sales of Silk Fabrics Sluggish

Overseas Silk Dispatches Not Transmitted… Prices Minor, Yet Nobody Inquires

Last week, both local and foreign silk markets in this port trended ever worse. The world's economies are showing signs of decline, sales of silk fabrics are still trending sluggish, not a few silk mills on both sides of the Pacific Ocean are shutting down or halting production, unemployed workers are rising daily, and consumption of raw silk is sharply declining. All overseas silk dispatches are not transmitted, silk prices are especially low, yet nobody inquires. The coldness of the European and American raw silk market has been unseen since the European war. Yokohama Japanese silk prices last week sharply fell to more than 700 Japanese yen. Shanghai mills, mills-agents, etc. are still just doing spot transactions, the futures market is quiet, and silk prices have the trend of sharply falling too. The transport of Japanese dry cocoons to Shanghai for sales has gotten very active. Though model cocoons have been transported, the Japanese silk traders, because they can see the mill silk's external sales don't move, the cocoon prices tread poorly. Japanese cocoons will halt transport to Shanghai. The Shanghai Silk Mill Trade Association and the Silk Cocoon General Office have both started to gather the silk and cocoon merchants to discuss means of resisting, in order to avoid encroaching sales of Chinese cocoons, and disrupting the market. Then, transport of Japanese cocoons to China is feared to not come to pass. Last week, spot silk transactions were 300 bags, exported were more than 800 bags, and overseas medium-lower body mills agents' raw silk prices are about to enter the 1000 tael territory. New York and Lyon Chinese silk prices are ever worse. Youth Garden

By the Fort of Taiwan 165

— Wen Juan

A tall, red Western-style house stands proudly amidst the boundless green fields. This is the campus of a certain university by the fort of Taiwan. Because I admired the seaside scenery and, incidentally, wanted to escape the summer heat, I resolutely moved here to spend my summer vacation. I initially thought that since the term was over, the air here would be quieter, but it turned out to be otherwise. Not only did many students from distant places not go home, but new students also arrived for the summer school. As a result, this Latin Quarter of Wusong became very lively.

Along the only stone path at the school gate, there are twenty to thirty low-rise bungalows, and a few are even covered with thatch, reminding one of the line, "Earthen walls and thatched roofs, a horse cherry tree in front of the door." Although there are no horse cherry trees here, there are a few weeping willows swaying in front of the eaves and fences, nestled between the red walls and green fields. While one cannot say that it is particularly beautiful, the signs of human habitation have almost completely disappeared.

The sole patrons of these bungalows and thatched cottages are the students of various schools, but nine out of ten are from China Public School. Other schools, such as the Merchant Marine Academy, are just there to make up the numbers. More than ten restaurants face each other, and they place their incredibly large dining tables on the road. The distance between one and the other is only three feet. Fortunately, there are no vehicles, and even if a few rickshaws arrive, they can still squeeze through. The owners of these restaurants are all from Henan, and they use clumsy stoves to make extremely unappetizing food and dishes, selling them to their patrons at very low prices. However, these patrons devour the food with gusto, as if they cannot get enough of the rich delicacies. Life as a student is truly made of gold. Even the digestive power of their stomachs surpasses everything else. I think that they are not only able to eat, but also able to make the most of their environment. In this humid coastal area, wearing leather shoes is both uncomfortable and prone to foot problems. So, they take off their leather shoes and simply do not wear socks, instead wearing a pair of clogs all day long. Even when they are at home, they only add a pair of shorts. I cannot describe their skin tone. In short, if an Indian were to pass by, he would definitely recognize them as fellow countrymen. When I first arrived here, I only heard the "da-la…da-la…" sound of clogs, and I almost suspected that I was in the Japanese countryside. But that was not the case. Their shoes were not Japanese clogs, but Cantonese wooden slippers. The style is very simple, and the price is cheap. They only sell for two dimes a pair in the small grocery stores in the Latin Quarter, and I doubt you can find such a high price anywhere else. It is said that this trend was initially promoted by Cantonese students, and gradually spread to students from other provinces. Now, all the students are following suit, except for a few female students. During the summer vacation, the students are not very studious. Their favorite activity is swimming. Anyway, the Huangpu River is not far away, and further away, one can go to the Three Gorges waters. They determine the distance of the location based on their swimming ability. Every day at sunset, when the bright moon has not yet emerged from the sea, one often sees teams of Cantonese or Sichuanese students walking down the dike to bathe. They usually do not swim very far. Only once did I see a Cantonese man swim from near the "flag house" to the lighthouse, about a mile away. Because the waters at the mouth of the Three Gorges are extremely turbulent, with the confluence of the Yangtze River and the Huangpu River, as well as the impact of the tides, people often drown. The last time a Merchant Marine Academy student, Xiang Yuzhi, died, it was in this area. So, people are wary and dare not easily go to "Shitang" anymore.

The seaside scenery is so beautiful. The morning glow dyes the seawater into various different, indescribable paintings. The weather in late summer and early autumn is just right, with a touch of coolness. Strolling along the embankment, one feels the wind in one's sleeves, bathed in such a solution of nature. Although it is not heaven, it is not something that exists in the human world either. In the evening, the powerful rays of the setting sun cast a myriad of colors across the sky. It kisses the seawater, making its cheeks flush red. At this time, male students with the "da-la" sound of clogs, carrying the graceful figures of female students, come to the seaside together for a walk. The sound of clogs and the "ge-ge" sound of high heels, combined with the crashing sound of the waves against the shore, create a wonderful symphony. This music should only exist on the sea, and cannot be heard elsewhere. In order to appreciate more of the beautiful scenery, they sit side by side on the seawall, talking about the past and the present, and all sorts of things that should be said between young people. However, the number of female students is less than 10% of the number of male students. So, many male students probably do not have girlfriends. I often say, "This is the land of men, and women are just ornaments." However, even so, their academic atmosphere is very good. Even if one person sits outside until late at night, there will be no unexpected incidents. Thinking back to the bitterness of not being able to sit freely in the French Park, I truly feel that this place and Shanghai are not in the same world. And, I do not hear any erhu tunes or the sounds of Beijing opera. Even in their dormitories outside the school, there is only some flute music. Unlike the apartment life in various universities in Beijing, where mahjong and Beijing opera are their only subjects, that kind of corrupt situation makes one feel unpleasant just thinking about it. However, the students here are not natives, but are gathered from all directions. But they are all very well-behaved and very serious. So, I think that the so-called power of the group is truly unbelievable.

I also lazily stay in such an environment, reading a few more good books.

A Healthy Woman 166

— (Hua Photo)

A New Atmosphere at Great China University 167

Great China University, with its short history and rapid development, is truly progressing by leaps and bounds. This is not an intentional compliment, but a genuine fact. Six years ago, over a hundred students and several teachers left Xiamen University and came to Shanghai. In such difficult circumstances, as President Wang of the university said, at the beginning, they rented houses and lived in narrow, simple dwellings that barely sheltered them from wind and rain. They borrowed money to eat, enduring hardship and struggling to make ends meet. Virtually nothing was available in terms of material necessities. At that time, could the people running the school, or anyone else, have imagined the Great China University of today? It is truly astonishing. In previous years, the student body was only two to three hundred, but the rate of increase has been very rapid. By last autumn, the number of students in all departments reached over 1,300. This year, about 200 students were admitted in the first round of admissions. Recently, in the second examination, over 500 students were admitted. What's most interesting is that on the day of this examination, men and women on Jiaozhou Road were bustling and crowded, and the large auditorium was filled with enthusiastic scenes. This goes without saying. From this, we can see the speed at which the number of students is increasing. It is also reported that the school will hold a third examination on September 5th. It is estimated that by the time school starts, the university will have 1,800 new and old students. This is not only a new era for Great China University, but also likely unprecedented among universities in Shanghai. In terms of school buildings, new buildings have been erected at Fanwangdu. There are eight towering Western-style buildings, with Qunxian Hall as the main auditorium, Qunce Hall as the first male dormitory, Qunli Hall as the second male dormitory, and Qunying Hall as the female dormitory. There is also a temporary office, a temporary chemical laboratory, faculty housing, a temporary auditorium, three large dining halls, a Western-style dining room, a coffee shop, etc., all exquisitely magnificent. In addition, there are more than ten bungalows, called "City Houses," for small-scale retail. This marks a new phase in the construction aspect of Great China University. In terms of equipment, a self-drilled artesian well and a water tower have been built in the west corner of the school. Reflectors have been installed in the classrooms, and automatic electric bells are installed on each floor. An electric clock is installed at the highest point of Qunxian Hall to avoid the inconvenience of shaking bells to signal class changes. All other utensils are mostly exquisite Chinese and Western items. Efforts are also being made to enrich the library and equipment. In addition, there is an old pool next to the university dormitory, which is currently being renovated and planned to be built as a swimming pool for male and female students to exercise during their spare time. In terms of classes, in addition to literature, science, commerce, law, teacher training, and preparatory courses, a kindergarten normal school has been added to create kindergarten teachers. There are also plans to open a kindergarten and primary school to promote elementary education and become a complete university. These plans are expected to be realized this semester. It is also heard that President Ou and others are planning to organize Great China New Village near the school buildings to design a new society. All of these are prominent aspects of the new atmosphere at Great China University. As for minor details, such as the fact that the Great China University girls of the past, not intentionally slandering them, did indeed have the flavor of sheltered young ladies, while the newly arrived girls are mostly generous and poised in social interactions, I don't need to list them all. In short, the Great China University of today is not the Great China University of the past, and the future progress of Great China University is still limitless. (Ze Xiang)

Page 23

Book and Newspaper Introductions

White Snake and Xu Xian 168

— Wen Zhi

— A One-Act Drama of Legend —

By Xiang Peiliang

"While it is true that some of the folk ideas in our Chinese society are poisoned by feudal thought, there are also those folk tales, legends, and ballads that aim for the survival, freedom, and prosperity of the nation, and a part of these certainly exist." In fact, many of those stories, legends, and ballads contain seeds of "national consciousness," and their content can very well represent the national character and national spirit of that era. If we say that this is a treasure trove of our literary expressions, it is by no means an exaggeration. However, very few Chinese literary writers have noticed these, and they are unwilling to explore these treasures.

China itself has always been a great enigma. Foreign scholars have even written books like "The Enigma of China," which shows that Chinese folk literature is extraordinarily rich. Unfortunately, most of it has been lost, except for the relatively memorable ones, and some have even been turned from gold into iron by ordinary bored people, losing their original form, and a true evaluation has never been given. Even after the New Literary Movement blossomed in China, there are still very few works that take folk stories, legends, and ballads as their subject matter. In terms of drama, it goes without saying. In principle, we cannot deny or despise these at all, but should collect them as much as possible and evaluate them, put the good ones into the art machine to give all the people a chance to appreciate them, and denounce and eliminate the bad ones as much as possible, so as to avoid repeating mistakes. Therefore, we should clearly recognize that the power of folk literature is endowed with the authority to penetrate the masses. Therefore, if we want our literature to truly expand to the masses and get their appreciation and response, we must absolutely not ignore the value of all folk literature.

This is very obvious. The first misuse of folk literature is in the old dramas with incomprehensible and lingering tastes, isn't it? The Weaver Girl and the Cowherd, The Legend of the White Snake, which of these dramas does not damage the original value by the general riffraff, and at the same time mislead so many people? But in the past, our writers were indifferent to this situation. After all, they still could not escape the ego-centered position. However, creating an exception, we found Xiang Peiliang's one-act drama "White Snake and Xu Xian" of folk legends on our literary scene, which is really worth praising. The story of White Snake and Xu Xian is very well known among the people. Every time during the Dragon Boat Festival, the actors who always appear on stage say that they are staging a show, but what is the content? It is difficult to say. Where is the true "White Snake and Xu Xian" original face being performed? Anyone who knows a little about drama will sigh in unison, right? Then Xiang Peiliang's work in this area is very meaningful. First, it opened up the precedent of expressing folk legends and reflecting them in drama. Second, it also gave a profound analysis of White Snake and Xu Xian, and evaluated their due value and position in "folk literature."

Regarding the legend of "White Snake and Xu Xian," although many people talk about it with relish, they have not finally recognized their great "love." Most of the views are like the guest in the play, "I think when Lady White was in the deep mountains before, how carefree and comfortable she was. She came to the world for no reason and almost lost her life several times. Now she doesn't know what the result will be. This is really self-inflicted trouble." And who can understand and sympathize like the daughter in the play, "I like Lady White, I love her love as deep as the sea, I love her courage as big as the sky, she just cares about love, she doesn't care about anything else, I also want to learn her boldness." "Love" is originally an interesting thing, but unfortunately most people misunderstand it, waste it in vain, and even destroy it. In the past, who had ever said such words for Bai Suzhen, "Emotions are such strange things, we used to have lively days too. I just need to use my magical powers to call stones to be our guests, and I can call the little birds in the mountains to turn into beautiful girls--these phantom-like things can also make us happy for a while, but I suddenly feel ridiculous, even terrifying, just like seeing too many activities of my own shadow, that kind of entertainment without heartfelt communication will not satisfy me, when their hands hold my hands, there is no warm feeling to excite my blood flow, on the day of the lake tour, I wanted to completely live in the world as a human being, I want to become a complete person to taste human emotions, I want to enjoy all the joys of the world, and also endure all the pains of the world, and at that time, we saw him, a innocent and glorious young man, so I decided to live my life with him." I think, about the passion of White Snake and Xu Xian, "Yes, you have already lost it, I exchanged it with my life, not just once, you are what I exchanged with my life several times," I am afraid that very few people have paid attention to it. Perhaps they will say as unreasonably as Fahai, "Why be obsessed with a demon, all that is fake--beauty, kindness, charm, are all on stage, all like lightning, there is great poison behind it, our life is like swimming, women are heavy objects that hinder you, make you fall into salt, and cannot reach the other shore safely, let alone a demon," really "don't know what our feelings are like." Therefore, I express my great respect for Xiang Peiliang's grasp of this great conclusion. In fact, only this is the true face of White Snake and Xu Xian that needs to be expressed.

Here, the author uses mature techniques, tight structure, and supporting foil to depict White Snake and Xu Xian. The characters used are very appropriate, and the content has not deviated from what is said in folk legends. I dare say that the author's "White Snake and Xu Xian" not only overthrows the old drama The Legend of the White Snake, but also opens up a different kind of color for our drama movement. Moreover, in the sense of drama education, it is also very profound, enough to stir people's "creative desire" and "upward will" to develop the great power of life. If this is used to replace and instill it into the people, the effect will be as expected.

Wilderness Poetry Special Issue 169

— Jiang Shiyan

The vigorous wilderness makes us readers more supportive and friendly. The efforts of the wilderness also make us work hard invisibly. Nationalism flies in our minds, national consciousness is fixed in our reason, and the needs of the nation are revealed before our eyes. We have clearly recognized it. We have long admired the articles of the wilderness. Its papers, creations, essays, poems, etc. are all beautiful in writing and bold in literary style, and especially Suizhuan and poems are the most. This time, the fifth issue of the third volume is a special issue of poetry, how happy and appreciative we are.

In the special issue of poetry, we discovered a new author. His poems directly make our hair stand on end, and they are short and only have four sections. Let's look at his work.

Go forward Zhang Xiamei

The bells of the times spur us not to hesitate, the decline of the nation does not allow us to be decadent again, prepare our blue blood and heads to fight for the nation, what is the glory of fighting to the death compared to a pile of yellow earth,

The sad horns keep wailing to urge us to mount our horses, the thousands of strands of soft silk are thrown away where the gun blades are exposed, oh, I only allow you a passionate kiss on the horse, wave your whip and go, I swear to stain the yellow sand with blood,

Cries do not hear the enemy's guns have attacked us, look at the martyrs' blood has flowed before us, hold up our sharp weapons and aim at the enemy, prepare our white bones to build the glory of our nation,

Go ahead friends, this is our time, don't shrink back, and don't pretend to hesitate, I'm holding a long gun, and you have to hold a short knife, if the enemy doesn't retreat, I swear to stain the yellow sand with blood,

Similarly, after reading this poem "Go Forward," there is another small poem by Bai Na to comfort the soldiers, "Dedicated to the Soldiers" is to encourage the soldiers to cheer up and go to the front for the nation, and to comfort the soldiers for sacrificing everything for the nation.

Soldiers,

Dedicate this lamp,

For you to attack the rebels,

……………………

Soldiers,

Sing generously,

And drink this cup and another cup,

……………………

Soldiers,

The bugle is playing,

Have you ever cheered up and shaken off your spirits,

After reading two generous and passionate encouragements and encouragements for the nation to go to the battlefield, our blood has already boiled, and our enthusiasm cannot be stopped. We feel that there is nothing in the world that is truly worth cherishing. We only cherish our nation, China, have 400 million compatriots felt the pain of the nation? I hope that this wilderness is universal in the world, and it will arouse the nationalistic center of the compatriots unconsciously, and cheer up the people's spirit. With the unity of the people, our nation is not afraid of the national flag everywhere, and all directions vibrate.

Tang Zengyang's "Ode to Youth in the Age" is different in style and meaning from the above two, and the warning is implicit in the joy. Now, copying down two sections can also see the different tones of the style and the neatness of the words.

The times sing of youth,

Birds chirp light songs,

Flowers and plants show a warm smile,

This is a holy land of happiness,

The times sing of youth,

The steeds gallop on the parade ground,

Millions of people sing before the distant mountains,

This is a holy land of happiness,

We have seen passionate heroic songs, we have seen brave words to encourage soldiers, we have seen beautiful and desolate recent works by Zengyang, and now we have seen another kind of ironic and cold "Urban Loose Strings" Fourth Target Field, Mi Luo is also an author we have long known, his works do not need our introduction. Now copy three sections below, and the readers can appreciate it themselves.

Such a desolate and deserted place with weeds and smoke, pitifully letting people fan their weapons and shoot targets, a grim aura of killing is lurking around the spikes and steel, obviously drawing a majestic and solemn divide,

This is a picture poem, the scenery of the target field suddenly leaps before our eyes, the weather, scenery, climate, and human feelings are truly revealed. Such a good place is indeed a scenic spot for us to embrace each other. It is a pity that you lovers who are holding hands and stepping into the park, have you ever heard the sound of "slap slap slap" of gunfire, and has infinite passion surged in your hearts, thinking of the land of your motherland, which has been occupied by foreign countries, and we are still going to appreciate it.

The rest include Wang Tiehua's "Whip Up Your Horse and Go Forward" and "The Chirp of the Stream," Huang Yuro's "Night Tour" "Not Allowed" Zengyang's "Praise Song," due to space limitations.

A Bird's-Eye View of New Works by European Writers (10) Last Chapter 170

— Manru

Novel by Norwegian Hamsun

Hamsun, who attracted much attention in European literary circles last year for his seventieth birthday, is now generally recognized as Norway's most important novelist. His recent work "The Last Chapter" (Det Sidste Lapital) was a sensation when it was first published, but we cannot help but admit that this book is very depressing. The managers of the Turlaas Sanatorium (the setting of the book) are really unfortunate, not only because they repeatedly encounter the tragic deaths of their guests, but also because the customers they attract are all terrible characters. It is rare to see such a group of people, all terribly uniform, and living in the same house. It is really rare to see a novel like "The Last Chapter," which is completely filled with sinister characters.

The central figure, who seems to be used as a mouthpiece by the author to some extent, is a person suspected of having suicidal tendencies. However, this person's attachment to life is enough to make him try to refuse to give up his room with a stove. I constantly complain about the poor food. When his wife, who had just reconciled with him, died in the fire because the sanatorium was burned down, his "suicide" only took the step of hanging a rope on a tree branch. And because he was busy taking out the pine needles in his socks and trying to stop the pain in his burned hand, he gave up his intention to commit suicide. This character seems very ridiculous, but we originally knew that he is the embodiment of the theme of the book. What is the theme of this book? That is, human beings have the will to survive. Even if "survival" is nothing to love and nothing to gain, people still eagerly cling to their survival and try to avoid the inevitable "last chapter"--the arrival of death.

We are all in the team, we can naturally change our garrison, but we cannot change our "god of war." But, ah, our good God, how much we oppose this matter. When the god of death walks to the door, we stand on tiptoe, shushing him, but when he holds us in his arms... we fight.

Of course, it won't be long before we fall, and then our spirit will inevitably decline. Later we were buried in the earth, so what are we trying to get rid of? Isn't it just to make those who have not died feel more comfortable?

The author is manipulating his puppets with a terrible humor, writing in his unique style, but his gloomy satire is failing to hit the mark, because when he makes us look at human beings from his small mirror, we see it, but we can't see any resemblance between these poor bugs and ourselves. As we think about it, if that sanatorium could make its customers die earlier, it would not only be beneficial to them, but also to the world. What are such people doing in the world?

Shanghai Market

Market News 171

The Great China Art Leather Shoe Company at the corner of Guangxi Road, west of the Grand Theatre on Sanma Road, declares that the company was founded by artist Cheng KeGuang and tycoon Lu Chengsheng. The company's men's and women's leather shoes of various styles are all striving for beauty and contain artistry. Therefore, not long after its opening, it has gained a great reputation in the social arena. In order to further beautify its products, the company specially announces a solicitation for Western and floral pattern paintings. Please invite national artists to contribute opinions publicly. The first prize is 60 yuan, the second prize is 30 yuan, the third prize is 15 yuan, the fourth to tenth prizes are 10 yuan each, and the eleventh to thirtieth prizes are 5 yuan each. Other applicants will also be given remuneration.

Wing On Company announces that the company's cosmetics department has newly arrived with a large batch of French perfumes and soaps, in various colors, which are fully prepared. Currently, it is the discount period. In addition to specially reducing the prices of each item, it has also added a one-yuan bargain department, such as French sandalwood body powder at 7.5 jiao per can, 2 cans per yuan, orchid hair tonic at 5.5 jiao per bottle, 3 bottles per yuan, mixed flower perfume at 4 jiao per bottle, 4 bottles per yuan, rose soap at 3.5 jiao per piece, 5 pieces per yuan, and German Baihua soap at 1.3 jiao per piece, 12 pieces per yuan. Such a huge sacrifice, cutting costs and selling at low prices, is really a rare opportunity in the sound of expensive gold and cheap silver. Customers are scrambling and extremely enthusiastic.

Guanshengyuan Food Company on Nanjing Road announces that the Guan Zhen Photo Studio attached to the second floor of the company's main store not only produces elegant and fashionable art photos, but also ordinary photos that are artistic and pleasing to the eye. In addition, the prices are low and uniform, with a 30% discount, so business is quite prosperous in Shanghai. Recently, the weather has turned cooler in autumn, and the school season for students is approaching again in autumn. The four-inch registration-style passports at 8 jiao for four photos and the small art photos at 4 jiao, are especially popular with people from all walks of life. The scene of crowded customers every day is quite like a market.
